ESKOOLIA SCHOOL ERP
Role & Permission Module
User Acceptance Testing (UAT) Report

PASS  (

1. Executive Summary
This report presents the findings of a comprehensive end-to-end User Acceptance Test (UAT) of the Role & Permission module in 
Eskoolia
 School ERP. Testing covered 50 test cases across 4 categories: Role CRUD (15), Permission Assignment (8), Access Control Enforcement (14), and UI/UX (13).
The module is in a partially functional state. Basic CRUD operations on roles work. However, a CRITICAL security vulnerability was discovered: permissions are enforced ONLY on the access-control API endpoints themselves. All other module APIs (students, fees, HR, finance, exams, library, inventory, 
behaviour
) have ZERO permission enforcement. A Teacher user with 0 assigned permissions can read, modify, and delete data across every module.
This means the permission system is purely cosmetic today — it controls UI sidebar visibility but does not enforce actual data access at the API layer.
Test Results Summary

2. Module Architecture
2.1 UI Pages
The Role Permission module has 4 frontend pages accessible from the sidebar navigation:
/
roles
 — Role list with Add/Edit/Delete and Assign Permission buttons
/roles/assign-permission — Module-based checkbox grid for assigning permissions to a role
/roles/login-permission — Enable/disable login access per user, with password reset
/roles/due-fees-login-permission — Block student/parent login based on unpaid fees
2.2 API Endpoints
Backend runs on Django REST Framework. All endpoints are under /
api
/v1/access-control/:

2.3 Data Model
Roles: 5 existing (Admin, Driver, Student, Super Admin, Teacher). Each role has an array of 
permission_ids
. Permissions: 96 total across 13 modules. Permission code format: 
module.entity
.verb
 (e.g., 
academics.add_
homework.view
). Available verbs: view, read, manage, add, edit, delete. User-Role assignments: 3 existing mappings (2 Teachers, 1 Driver).
3. Detailed Test Results
3.1 Role CRUD Operations

4. Critical Issues & Bugs
4.1 [CRITICAL] No Backend Permission Enforcement on Module APIs
Severity: CRITICAL | Priority: P0 | Affects: ALL modules
The permission system only gates the access-control endpoints (roles, permissions). Every other API endpoint (students, fees, HR, payroll, finance, exams, library, inventory, 
behaviour
, admissions) performs NO permission check. A user with the Teacher role and ZERO permissions assigned can: read all student records, read all financial data, read all HR/payroll records, and even DELETE student records. This makes the entire permission system cosmetic — it hides sidebar items in the UI but does not protect data at the API layer.
Recommendation: Implement a DRF permission class (e.g., HasModulePermission) that checks the user's role permissions on every API view. Apply it globally via DEFAULT_PERMISSION_CLASSES in settings.py.
4.2 [CRITICAL] Permission Granularity is View-Only
Severity: CRITICAL | Priority: P1
Of 96 permissions, most only have a 'view' verb. Only the 
admin_section
 module has add/edit/delete granularity. This means even if backend enforcement existed, you cannot grant a 
Teacher
 'view students' without also implicitly granting 'delete students'. The permission model needs CRUD-level granularity for every module entity.
4.3 [FAIL] Duplicate Role Name Returns 500
Severity: HIGH | Priority: P2
Creating a role with a name that already exists returns HTTP 500 (internal server error) instead of 400 with a user-friendly validation message. The database unique constraint fires but is not caught by the API serializer.
4.4 [FAIL] GET/DELETE Non-existent Role Returns 500
Severity: MEDIUM | Priority: P2
Requesting GET or DELETE on a role ID that does not exist returns HTTP 500 instead of 404 Not Found. The view is not handling 
DoesNotExist
 exceptions.
4.5 [FAIL] Assign Permission URL Parameter Ignored
Severity: MEDIUM | Priority: P3
Navigating to /roles/assign-permission/2 (Teacher) always loads Admin (id=1) permissions. The URL path parameter is ignored; the frontend always defaults to the first role in the dropdown.
4.6 [FAIL] Due Fees Login Permission Page Non-Functional
Severity: HIGH | Priority: P2
The Due Fees Login Permission page has two bugs: (1) The Section dropdown shows all 36 sections from all classes instead of filtering by selected class. (2) Clicking Search with a class selected makes no API call and returns empty results. The search functionality appears to be unimplemented or broken.
4.7 [FAIL] No Confirmation Dialog on Role Delete
Severity: MEDIUM | Priority: P3
Clicking the Delete button on a role performs the deletion immediately without any confirmation prompt. This is a destructive action that should require user confirmation.
4.8 [FAIL] Empty Form Submit Shows No Validation
Severity: LOW | Priority: P4
Submitting the Add Role form with an empty name field silently fails with no visual feedback. Should show inline validation or a toast message.
5. Improvement Recommendations
5.1 Backend Permission Enforcement (P0)
Create a custom DRF permission class that maps each API 
viewset
 to its required permission codes. Example: 
StudentsViewSet
 requires 
student_
info.student
_
list.view
 for GET, 
student_info.add_student.add
 for POST, etc. Register it in DEFAULT_PERMISSION_CLASSES so it applies globally. This single change would close the biggest security gap.
5.2 Expand Permission Granularity (P1)
Current state: 96 permissions, mostly view-only. Target state: ~300+ permissions with full CRUD verbs (view, add, edit, delete) for every module entity. Generate these programmatically from the model registry. Example: for the 
Students
 module, 
create:
 
students.student
_
list.view
, 
students.student_list.add
, 
students.student
_
list.edit
, 
students.student
_
list.delete
, 
students.student
_
category.view
, 
students.student_category.add
, etc.
5.3 Role Templates & Hierarchy
Add pre-built role templates (Principal, Vice Principal, Class Teacher, Subject Teacher, Accountant, Librarian, Transport Manager, Parent, Student) with sensible default permissions. Implement role hierarchy so a 
Principal
 inherits all Teacher permissions automatically.
5.4 Audit Logging
Every permission change, role assignment, and login permission toggle should be logged with timestamp, actor, action, and before/after values. This is essential for compliance in educational institutions.
5.5 API Error Handling
Replace all 500 errors with proper 400/404/409 responses. Use DRF exception handlers to catch 
IntegrityError
 (duplicate names), 
DoesNotExist
 (invalid IDs), and return structured error JSON with user-readable messages.
5.6 UI Improvements
Add confirmation dialogs for all destructive actions (delete role, remove permissions). Show inline validation on form fields. Fix the section dropdown cascading filter on Due Fees page. Show toast notifications on success/failure. Add bulk permission assignment (e.g., 'Grant all view permissions').
6. AI Integration Recommendations
If Claude were building this system to production-grade standards, these AI-powered features would set it apart from every competing school ERP:
6.1 AI-Powered Role Recommendation Engine
When creating a new staff member and assigning them a role, the system should use AI to analyze their job title, department, and responsibilities, then automatically recommend a role with pre-selected permissions. For example, entering 'Chemistry Lab Assistant' would suggest the Teacher role with academics, examination (view-only), and 
student_info
 (view-only) permissions, but NOT fees, HR, or finance access. 
The AI
 considers the 
principle
 of least privilege.
6.2 Anomaly Detection on Permission Usage
Train a model on normal access patterns per role. Flag anomalies in real-time: a 
Teacher
 accessing finance APIs at 2 AM, a Driver downloading the full student list, or a 
Student
 role making 500 API calls in an hour. Display alerts on the admin dashboard and optionally auto-revoke sessions. This catches both insider threats and compromised accounts.
6.3 Natural Language Permission Queries
Allow admins to ask questions like 'Who can delete student records?' or 'What can the Driver role access?' and get instant, accurate answers by querying the permission graph. Extend this to 'Show me everyone who accessed fee data in the last week' for audit purposes. Implementation: an LLM tool-use agent backed by 
the permission
 and audit log APIs.
6.4 Smart Permission Conflict Detection
When an admin assigns permissions, AI should flag conflicts and risks: 'Granting 
fee_payment.add
 to the 
Student
 role allows students to create fake payment records. Are you sure?' or 'The Teacher role has 
delete_student
 but no 
view_student
 — this combination is likely a mistake.' This prevents misconfiguration at the point of entry.
6.5 Automated Compliance Reporting
Generate periodic reports: 'These 3 staff members have permissions they have never used in 90 days — consider revoking.' 'The 
Accountant
 role was granted HR access on Jan 
15
 but this was never approved in the change log.' 'All parent accounts have 
correct
 fee-based login restrictions.' This replaces manual quarterly audits.
6.6 AI-Driven Onboarding Wizard
When a new school starts using the ERP, an AI wizard interviews the principal about their organizational structure: How many departments? Do class teachers handle attendance? Does the accountant also manage inventory? Based on answers, it auto-generates the complete role and permission structure, saving days of manual setup.
7. Conclusion & Verdict
The Role & Permission module has solid foundational architecture: clean API design, JWT authentication, module-based permission grouping, and a functional UI for basic role management. However, it has a showstopper security flaw: permissions are not enforced at the API layer beyond the access-control endpoints themselves.
Until backend permission enforcement is implemented across ALL module APIs, the system CANNOT be used in production. Any authenticated user can access and modify any data in any module, regardless of their assigned role and permissions.
The recommended priority order is: (1) Backend permission enforcement on all APIs. (2) Expand permission granularity to CRUD per entity. (3) Fix API error handling (500s to 400/404). (4) Fix UI bugs (Due Fees page, URL params, validation). (5) Add audit logging. (6) Implement AI-powered features for competitive differentiation.
With these improvements, the module would meet enterprise-grade standards suitable for school ERP deployment. The AI integration recommendations would position 
Eskoolia
 as the most intelligent school management platform on the market.
